ہوگا۔ یعنی متولی کواپنے وقت تاوان دینا پڑے گا ۔ ابوبکر رازی سے مروی ہے کہ ہمارے زمانہ میں ظالموں کے خوف سے بچا ہوا مال عمارت کے استحکام کے دو اور ہیں
Chapter on what invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. There is no harm in decorating the mosque with plaster, teak, and gold water. His statement 'no harm' indicates that he will not be rewarded nor sin. It is said it is a devotion. This is when done from one's own wealth. As for the trustee, he does from waqf property what strengthens the building, not decoration; if he does, he is liable. And Allah knows best. Commentary: There is disagreement. Some consider decoration makruh. Ali passed by a decorated mosque and asked whose it was. The Prophet counted three things that cause destruction. Waleed spent wealth on Medina mosque, and Umar ibn Abdul Aziz gave it to poor. These are proofs for dislike. Hanafis see no harm, citing Umar's expansion and decoration, and that decoration encourages i'tikaf. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said the author's 'no harm' means no reward or sin. Some say it is worship, as Allah commands building mosques. The Kaaba is decorated with gold and silk. Ibn al-Humam said it is worship because it honors mosques. The author says it is worship or permissible only when done from personal wealth, not waqf. The trustee must only strengthen the building; otherwise he is liable. Abu Bakr al-Razi narrated that in our time, using money saved from unjust rulers for strengthening is permissible.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on decorating mosques. The matn (original text) states that there is no harm (la ba's) in decorating mosques with plaster, teak, and gold water. The commentator explains that 'no harm' means the act is neither rewarded nor sinful—it is neutral. Some scholars consider it a devotional act (qurba). However, this applies only when done from one's own lawful wealth. If a trustee (mutawalli) uses waqf funds for decoration instead of structural maintenance, he becomes liable for compensation. The commentary then presents the difference of opinion: some early scholars (like Ali and others) considered decoration makruh, citing hadith about three destructive things and the example of Waleed. But the Hanafi school, based on the practice of Umar al-Faruq who expanded and decorated the mosque, and the reasoning that decoration encourages people to sit in the mosque for i'tikaf, holds it permissible. The author of Al-Hidayah, Al-Marghinani, clarifies that the permissibility or reward depends on the source of funds. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi also confirms the neutral ruling. The passage ends with a narration from Abu Bakr al-Razi that using money saved from oppressive rulers for strengthening the mosque is permissible, implying the trustee would not be liable in that case. Thus, the Hanafi position is that mosque decoration is permissible (mubah) but not an encouraged act of worship, and it must be funded from personal or permissible sources, not waqf endowments meant for structural integrity.

Key Terms
لا بأس (la ba's): A legal term meaning 'no harm' or 'permissible', indicating the act is neither obligatory nor prohibited, and carries no reward or sin.
متولي (mutawalli): The trustee or administrator of a waqf (endowment), responsible for managing its property and disbursing funds according to the founder's stipulations.
ضامن (damin): Liable or responsible for compensation; in this context, the mutawalli must reimburse the waqf for misused funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in Al-Hidayah, what is the ruling on decorating a mosque with plaster and gold water?
A) It is haram and sinful.
B) It is makruh and discouraged.
C) It is permissible but neither rewarded nor sinful, if done from personal wealth.
D) It is a recommended act of worship (sunnah).

Key Takeaway
Mosque decoration is mubah in the Hanafi school, but only when funded from personal wealth; the mutawalli must not use waqf funds for beautification lest he become liable for compensation.

Method of Performing Sajdah Tilawah
Ruling on the method of sajdah tilawah with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of performing sajdah tilawah and explain why no tashahhud or salam is required.

Core Idea
Sajdah tilawah: takbir without raising hands, sujud, then takbir, with no tashahhud or salam.

This passage from al-Hidayah outlines the exact method for performing the wajib act of sajdah tilawah. It also clarifies that the two takbirs are sunnah (not wajib) and that, unlike prayer, no tashahhud or salam follows. The reasoning is based on qiyas to prayer sujud and the practice of Ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sajdah tilawah is wajib upon reciting or hearing a prostration verse. The passage describes the method to correctly fulfill this obligation.
The act is separate from prayer; it has its own rules.
2
List the steps of the method
Upon intending sajdah tilawah: (1) say 'Allahu Akbar' without raising hands, (2) perform one prostration (sajdah), (3) say 'Allahu Akbar' while raising the head.
These steps are explicitly stated in the source.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas to the prostration in prayer (sajdah al-salah) and a report from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (ra).
Qiyas jaliy is used: the common element is prostration itself.
4
Understand the reasoning for no tashahhud/salam
Tashahhud and salam are for exiting prayer (tahallul), which requires a prior tahrimah (opening takbir). Since sajdah tilawah has no tahrimah, there is no need for tahallul.
The concept of tahrimah is central to this distinction.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on what to recite
The text is silent on what to say during prostration. Two opinions exist: recite the same as in prayer sujud, or a specific phrase related to the verse. This is a minor internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi is to recite what one normally recites in sujud of prayer.

ومن اراد السجود كبر ولم يرفع يديه وسجد ثم كبر و رفع رأسه اعتبار بسجدة الصلوة وهو المروع عن کہ آیت کی ابن مسعود و لا تشهد عليه و لا سلام لان ذلك للتحلل و هو يستدعى سبق التحريمة و هي منعدمة
ترجمہ اور جن نے سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو وہ تکبیر کہے اور ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے اور سجدہ کرے پھر تکبیر کہہ کر اپنا سر اٹھا لے نماز کے نے محیط کے سجدہ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہی ابن مسعودؓ سے مروی ہے اور اس پر نہ تشہد ہے اور نہ سلام ہے کیونکہ سلام تو نماز سے نکلنے کے لئے ہے ہیں تو مشار اور وہ تقاضا کرتا ہے سبقت تحریمہ کا اور تحریمہ معدوم ہے۔ تشریح. اس عبارت میں سجدہ تلاوت کی کیفیت کا بیان ہے سو کیفیت یہ ہے کہ جب سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کا ارادہ ہوتو بغیر دونوں بانو اٹھائے تکبیر کہہ کر سجدہ کرے پھر تکبیر کہہ کر اپنا سر زمین سے اٹھا لے۔ دلیل: نماز کے سجدہ پر قیاس ہے یہی عبد اللہ ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعال عنہ سے مروی ہے یہ ذہن میں رہے کہ یہ دونوں تکبیریں مسنون ہیں واجب نہیں ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ سجدہ تلاوت کرنے والے پر نہ تشہد ہے نہ سلام ہے کیونکہ تشہد اور سلام نماز سے نکلنے کے لئے مشروع ہوئے ہیں اور نماز سے نکلنا تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ پہلے تحریمہ ہوا۔ کرنے کے کریمہ اس جگہ معدوم ہے پس جب تحریمہ معدوم ہے تو تحلل بھی نہیں ہوگا اور جب تحلل نہیں ہے تو تشہد اور سلام بھی نہیں ہوں گے۔ فوائد قدوری اور ہدایہ کی عبارت اس بارے میں خاموش ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت میں کیا پڑھے ۔ سو اس سلسلے میں بعض نے تو یہ کہا ہے ؟ نماز کے سجدہ میں جو پڑھا جاتا ہے وہی تلاوت میں پڑھے اور بعض کا قول ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت میں یہ کہے سبحان ربنا ان كان وعد رمضان کے
Method of performing prostration. Translation: He said... And the scholars said... Explanation: Verse of prostration, turning away, there is no [issue], verses are equal, without wudu. And whoever intends to perform prostration should say takbir and not raise his hands, prostrate, then say takbir and raise his head, drawing analogy to the prostration of prayer, and this is reported from Ibn Mas'ud. And there is no tashahhud and no salam, because that is for exiting (the prayer), and that requires the preceding tahrimah (opening takbir), and tahrimah is absent. Explanation: This passage describes the manner of sajdah tilawah. So the manner is that when one intends to perform sajdah tilawah, without raising both hands, say takbir and prostrate, then say takbir and raise the head from the ground. Proof: analogized to the prostration of prayer. This is reported from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). It should be noted that these two takbirs are sunnah, not wajib. The author of al-Hidayah says: The one performing sajdah tilawah does not have tashahhud or salam, because tashahhud and salam are legislated for exiting prayer, and exiting prayer requires that tahrimah be present first. Tahrimah is absent here, so when tahrimah is absent, tahallul (exit) does not occur, and when tahallul does not occur, there will be no tashahhud or salam. Benefits: The texts of al-Quduri and al-Hidayah are silent about what to recite during sajdah tilawah. So in this regard, some said that one should recite what is recited in the prostration of prayer, and some say that during sajdah tilawah one should say 'Subhana rabbana in kana wa'du Ramadan...'
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the method of performing sajdah tilawah. The ruling states that upon intending sajdah tilawah, one should say the takbir (Allahu Akbar) without raising the hands, then prostrate, then say another takbir while raising the head. The proof (dalil) is qiyas to the prostration in prayer, and it is also reported from Ibn Mas'ud (ra). Importantly, the two takbirs are sunnah, not wajib; missing them does not invalidate the sajdah. The passage also clarifies that there is no tashahhud or salam after sajdah tilawah, because tashahhud and salam are for exiting the prayer, which requires the prior presence of tahrimah (the opening takbir that initiates prayer). Since sajdah tilawah outside prayer has no tahrimah, there is no tahallul (exit), hence no tashahhud or salam. A beneficial note (fa'idah) mentions that the classical texts are silent on what to recite during the sajdah. Two opinions are given: recite the same as in prayer sujud, or recite a specific phrase 'Subhana rabbana in kana wa'du Ramadan...' (which appears to be a partial quote from the Quranic verse of promise).

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates prayer and makes acts forbidden (haram) that were previously permissible.
تحلل (tahallul): The act of exiting prayer, typically with salam.
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdah tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran (ayat al-sajdah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method, what is the ruling on raising hands during the takbir for sajdah tilawah?
A) It is sunnah to raise hands.
B) It is wajib to raise hands.
C) It is not done (the hands are not raised).
D) It is recommended but not required.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah is performed with two takbirs (sunnah), one prostration, and no tashahhud or salam, analogized to prayer sujud and reported from Ibn Mas'ud.

Linguistic Definition of Janaza and Chapter Placement
Defines janaza and explains chapter order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term 'janaza' correctly and explain why the chapter on funerals is placed at the end of the book of prayer.

Core Idea
Janaza means deceased or bier; the chapter order ends with a source of blessing.

This passage opens the chapter on funerals by clarifying the primary term 'janaza' and addressing a potential question about the order of topics. Understanding the linguistic distinction and the author's pedagogical intent helps you navigate funeral rulings with context.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two readings of janaza
Identify that 'janaza' with fatha on the jim refers to the deceased person, while with kasra it refers to the bier. This terminological clarity is essential for precise reading of later texts.
Memorize: fatha = deceased, kasra = bier.
2
Understand the reason for chapter placement
The author states death is the final occurrence, so funeral prayer is mentioned last. This follows the chronological order of life events.
3
Answer the objection about prayer inside the Ka'bah
The objection: why wasn't prayer inside the Ka'bah placed before funerals? The answer: it was placed at the end of Kitab al-Salah to end on a note of blessing and tranquility.
This shows attention to tarteeb and barakah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنائز ترجمہ یہ باب جنازوں کے احکام کے بیان میں ہے تشریح جنائز، جنازہ کی جمع ہے جنازہ جیم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ میت کے لئے مستعمل ہے اور کسرہ کے ساتھ اس تخت کے لئے مستعمل ہے جس پر میت کو رکھا جاتا ہے موت چونکہ آخری عارض ہے اس لئے نماز جنازہ کو سب سے آخر میں بیان کیا ہے لیکن اگر کوئی یہ کہہ دے کہ صلوۃ فی کعبہ کو اس سے پہلے ذکر کرنا چاہئے تھا حالانکہ اس کے بعد ذکر کیا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صلوۃ فی الکعبہ کو کتاب الصلوۃ کے آخر میں اس لئے ذکر کیا گیا ہے تا کہ کتاب الصلوۃ کا خاتمہ ایسی چیز سے ہو جسکے ساتھ حالا اور مسکا نا تبرک حاصل کیا جاتا ہے میت پر نماز جنازہ پڑھنے کی وجہ عقل کا تقاضا ہے کہ جب کسی انسان کو بہت سے آدمیوں کا گروہ کسی عالیشان حاکم کے آگے لے جا کر اس کے لئے سفارش کریں اور اس کی معافی کی درخواست کریں اور اس کے لئے گڑ گڑا کر التجاء کریں تو بالآخر اس کا قصور معاف ہو جاتا ہے یہی نماز جنازہ کا راز ہے یعنی نماز جنازہ اس لئے مقرر کی گئی ہے کہ مومنیں کے ایک گروہ کا میت کی سفارش میں شریک ہونا اس پر رحمت الہی کے ناز ہونے میں بڑا کامل اثر رکھتا ہے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم فرماتے ہیں ما من مسلم يموت فيقوم على جنازيه اربعون رجلا لا يشركون بالله شيا الا شفعهم الله فيه یعنی کوئی آدمی مسلمان ایسا نہیں مرتا ہے کہ اس کے جنازہ پر چالیس آدمی کھڑے ہوں جو خدا کے ساتھ کسی کو شریک نہ کرتے ہوں مگر اس میت کے حق میں ان کی سفارش قبول کرتا ہے شرح اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب آدمی کی روح بدن کو چھوڑتی ہے تو اس کی حس مشترک وغیرہ کو حس اور اور اک باقی رہتا ہے اور جو خیالات اور علوم اس کے ساتھ تجھے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ہمراہ رہتے ہیں اور پھر عالم بالا سے اور علوم کا اس پر ترشح ہوتا ہے جن کی وجہ سے بہت کو عذاب یا ثواب ہوتا ہے پس خدا تعالیٰ کے نیک بندوں کی ہمتیں جب عالم قدس تک پہنچتی ہیں اور اس میت کے لئے وہ گڑ گڑا کر دعا کرتے ہیں یا میت کے لئے بہت کچھ صدقہ دیتے ہیں تو حکم اسی سے میت کے حق میں وہ نافع پڑتا ہے
Chapter of Funerals. Translation: This chapter discusses the rulings of funerals. Commentary: 'Jana'iz' is the plural of 'janaza'. With fatha on the jim, it refers to the deceased; with kasra, it refers to the bier on which the deceased is placed. Since death is the final occurrence, the funeral prayer is mentioned last. But if someone says that prayer inside the Ka'bah should have been mentioned before it, while it was mentioned after, the answer is that prayer inside the Ka'bah was mentioned at the end of Kitab al-Salah so that the book ends with something through which happiness and tranquility are obtained. The reason for offering funeral prayer over the deceased is a rational requirement: when a group of people take a person before a great ruler, intercede for him, ask for forgiveness, and plead earnestly, ultimately his fault is forgiven. This is the secret of the funeral prayer: a group of believers sharing in intercession for the deceased has a great effect in bringing down divine mercy. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no Muslim who dies and forty men who do not associate anything with Allah stand over his funeral but that Allah accepts their intercession for him.' The explanation of this is that when the soul leaves the body, the common sense and other senses remain, and thoughts and knowledge remain with it, and then from the higher world, more knowledge emanates upon it, due to which there is punishment or reward. Then when the noble servants of Allah reach the holy realm and plead for the deceased or give charity, that becomes beneficial for the deceased.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the chapter on funerals (Bab al-Jana'iz). It begins by defining the term 'janaza' linguistically. The author explains why the funeral prayer is placed at the end of the book, answering a potential objection about the order. The main point is the rational wisdom behind funeral prayer: it is like intercession before a ruler, and the Prophet's hadith about forty sincere believers guarantees acceptance of intercession. The commentary then explains how prayers and charity benefit the deceased, drawing on the continued existence of the soul and its ability to perceive.

Key Terms
جنازہ (janaza): With fatha on jim: the deceased person. With kasra: the bier on which the deceased is carried.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author place the chapter on funerals at the end of the Book of Prayer?
A) Because death is the final occurrence in a person's life.
B) Because funeral rulings are less important.
C) Because prayer inside the Ka'bah was already covered.
D) Because the funeral prayer is not a prayer.

Key Takeaway
Janaza has two meanings (deceased or bier) distinguished by vowel, and the chapter is placed last for chronological and barakah reasons.

The Wisdom and Virtue of Funeral Prayer
Explains the wisdom of funeral prayer and cites hadith on intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rational wisdom behind funeral prayer and state the hadith condition for intercession.

Core Idea
Funeral prayer is intercession; forty sincere believers guarantee acceptance.

This passage unveils the profound wisdom behind the funeral prayer: it is a collective intercession before Allah, analogous to pleading before a ruler. The Prophet's hadith assures that forty believers free from shirk secure forgiveness for the deceased, highlighting the great effect of communal prayer and charity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rational analogy
The author likens funeral prayer to a group interceding before a great ruler. This rational parallel shows why funeral prayer is prescribed: it invokes mercy through collective supplication.
Think of the ruler as Allah, the intercessors as believers.
2
Memorize the hadith and its condition
The hadith states: 'No Muslim dies and forty men who do not associate anything with Allah stand over his funeral but that Allah accepts their intercession for him.' Note the condition: forty men, free of shirk.
The hadith is found in Muslim and others.
3
Appreciate the spiritual mechanism
After death, the soul retains senses and knowledge; prayers and charity reach the deceased. This explains why intercession benefits the dead.
This reinforces the importance of attending funerals and making du'a.

Source Text

باب الجنائز ترجمہ یہ باب جنازوں کے احکام کے بیان میں ہے تشریح جنائز، جنازہ کی جمع ہے جنازہ جیم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ میت کے لئے مستعمل ہے اور کسرہ کے ساتھ اس تخت کے لئے مستعمل ہے جس پر میت کو رکھا جاتا ہے موت چونکہ آخری عارض ہے اس لئے نماز جنازہ کو سب سے آخر میں بیان کیا ہے لیکن اگر کوئی یہ کہہ دے کہ صلوۃ فی کعبہ کو اس سے پہلے ذکر کرنا چاہئے تھا حالانکہ اس کے بعد ذکر کیا ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صلوۃ فی الکعبہ کو کتاب الصلوۃ کے آخر میں اس لئے ذکر کیا گیا ہے تا کہ کتاب الصلوۃ کا خاتمہ ایسی چیز سے ہو جسکے ساتھ حالا اور مسکا نا تبرک حاصل کیا جاتا ہے میت پر نماز جنازہ پڑھنے کی وجہ عقل کا تقاضا ہے کہ جب کسی انسان کو بہت سے آدمیوں کا گروہ کسی عالیشان حاکم کے آگے لے جا کر اس کے لئے سفارش کریں اور اس کی معافی کی درخواست کریں اور اس کے لئے گڑ گڑا کر التجاء کریں تو بالآخر اس کا قصور معاف ہو جاتا ہے یہی نماز جنازہ کا راز ہے یعنی نماز جنازہ اس لئے مقرر کی گئی ہے کہ مومنیں کے ایک گروہ کا میت کی سفارش میں شریک ہونا اس پر رحمت الہی کے ناز ہونے میں بڑا کامل اثر رکھتا ہے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم فرماتے ہیں ما من مسلم يموت فيقوم على جنازيه اربعون رجلا لا يشركون بالله شيا الا شفعهم الله فيه یعنی کوئی آدمی مسلمان ایسا نہیں مرتا ہے کہ اس کے جنازہ پر چالیس آدمی کھڑے ہوں جو خدا کے ساتھ کسی کو شریک نہ کرتے ہوں مگر اس میت کے حق میں ان کی سفارش قبول کرتا ہے شرح اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب آدمی کی روح بدن کو چھوڑتی ہے تو اس کی حس مشترک وغیرہ کو حس اور اور اک باقی رہتا ہے اور جو خیالات اور علوم اس کے ساتھ تجھے مرنے کے بعد اس کے ہمراہ رہتے ہیں اور پھر عالم بالا سے اور علوم کا اس پر ترشح ہوتا ہے جن کی وجہ سے بہت کو عذاب یا ثواب ہوتا ہے پس خدا تعالیٰ کے نیک بندوں کی ہمتیں جب عالم قدس تک پہنچتی ہیں اور اس میت کے لئے وہ گڑ گڑا کر دعا کرتے ہیں یا میت کے لئے بہت کچھ صدقہ دیتے ہیں تو حکم اسی سے میت کے حق میں وہ نافع پڑتا ہے

Recommended Actions for the Dying Person
Provides rulings on positioning the dying person, talqeen, and post-death actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions for a dying person and their proofs according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The dying person is laid on the right side facing the qibla; talqeen of the shahada is Sunnah.

This passage from Al-Quduri discusses the etiquettes of death in Islam. The rulings are based on analogy to burial and a hadith. We will explore the positions and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended position for the dying person
The matn states the dying person should be turned to face the qibla on his right side. This is the Sunnah position.
The basis is analogy to the grave position.
2
Understand the alternative position
In some lands, laying supine is chosen due to ease. This is a concession, not the primary Sunnah.
The author of Hidayah mentions this.
3
Derive the ruling for talqeen
The hadith 'Prompt your dying ones with the shahada' provides the proof. The imperative indicates recommendation (Sunnah) not obligation.
The dying person should not be ordered to repeat it.
4
Identify post-death actions
After death, the jaw is tied and eyes closed. These are recommended.
These actions are part of the sunnah.

قریب المرگ کو کس ہیئت پر لٹایا جائے اذا احتضر الرجل وجه الى القبلة على شقه الايمن اعتبارا بحال الوضع فى القبر لانه اشرف عليه والمختار في بلادنا الاستلقاء لانه ايسر لخروج الروح والاول هو السنة ولقن How to lay the person nearing death. When a man is dying, he should be turned to face the qibla on his right side, considering the position in the grave because that is more honorable (for him). And the chosen practice in our lands is to lay him supine because it is easier for the soul to exit, and the first is the Sunnah. He should be prompted with the two testimonies because of the saying: 'Prompt your dying ones with the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' And by 'dying ones' are meant those near death. Then when he dies, his jaw is tied and his eyes are closed. With this, inheritance becomes operative. Then there is beautification of the deceased's appearance, which is commendable. Commentary: Al-Quduri used the word 'ihtadara' for nearing death, meaning the dying person is called [muhtadar] either because death approaches him or because the angels of death are present. Signs of death are that the near-death person's both feet become loose, he cannot stand, his nose becomes crooked, and the skin of his forehead stretches. Anyway, the practice for near death is to lay the deceased on his right side facing the qibla because that is the Sunnah position for placing in the grave, so by analogy, the near-death is also placed in that position because this person is about to go to the grave. The author of Hidayah says: 'In our lands of Transoxiana, laying supine is chosen because this position is easier for the exit of the soul. In this case, a pillow or something high is placed under the head so that his face is towards the qibla, not towards the sky. But there is no text for this position, only reason, which is not considered. Therefore, the author said that the first is Sunnah, i.e., laying on the side is Sunnah. The second practice is to prompt the dying with the testimonies, i.e., sit near him and recite aloud: 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasulullah.' He should not order the dying person to recite it because that is a time of extreme difficulty.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the recommended actions for the dying person. The matn from Al-Quduri states: when a man is dying (muhtadhar), he should be turned to face the qibla on his right side, analogizing to the position in the grave. However, in some regions like Transoxiana, the preferred practice (mukhtar) is to lay him supine with a pillow to tilt his face toward the qibla, as it is easier for the soul to leave. The author (Ashraf al-Hadaya) upholds the first as Sunnah but acknowledges the local custom. After death, the jaw is tied and eyes closed. Then the deceased's appearance is beautified. Talqeen (prompting) of the shahada is commanded by a hadith, but the dying person should not be ordered to repeat it, just reminded, due to their condition.

Key Terms
تلقین (talqeen): Prompting the dying person to say or hear the shahada, without commanding them to repeat it.
احتضر (ihtadara): Derived from hadara (to be present), meaning the person is in the throes of death, with death or angels present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) On the left side facing the qibla
B) On the right side facing the qibla
C) Flat on the back facing upward
D) Sitting upright facing the qibla

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah for the dying is to be laid on the right side facing the qibla, and to be prompted with the shahada without being commanded to repeat it.

Positioning the Dying Person: Sunnah and Practical Concession
Ruling on positioning the dying person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on positioning the dying person and explain the reason for the practical preference of laying on the back.

Core Idea
Turning the dying to face the qibla is Sunnah, but laying on the back is permitted for ease of passing.

The dying person's final moments are sacred. The Hanafi school teaches that turning him to face the qibla on his right side is the Sunnah, by analogy with the grave. However, recognizing the difficulty of the soul's departure, scholars in Transoxiana adopted laying on the back as the easier method. Let's examine the reasoning behind these practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Positioning the dying person. What is the hukm? It is sunnah muakkadah to turn him on his right side facing the qibla.
The text states 'والأول هو السنة'.
2
Locate the dalil
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to the placement of the deceased in the grave: just as the dead are laid on their right side facing qibla, so should the dying, because that state is more honorable.
The phrase 'اعتبارا بحال الوضع فى القبر' indicates the analogy.
3
Note the practical concession
In Transoxiana, the chosen practice (المختار) is to lay the dying on his back because it is easier for the soul to exit. This is not a replacement of the Sunnah but a permissible alternative for ease.
The text says 'لانه ايسر لخروج الروح'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling today is that both positions are valid, but laying on the back is the common practice due to ease, while acknowledging that the right side is the Sunnah.
The author does not specify a tarjih authority, but the practice is widespread.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اذا احتضر الرجل وجه الى القبلة على شقه الايمن اعتبارا بحال الوضع فى القبر لانه اشرف عليه والمختار في بلادنا الاستلقاء لانه ايسر لخروج الروح والاول هو السنة ولقن الشهادتين لقوله لقنوا موتاكم شهادة ان لا اله الا الله والمراد الذى قرب من الموت فاذا مات شد لحياه وغمض عيناه بذلک جری التوارث ثم فيه تحسينة فيستحسن
When a man is on the verge of death, he is turned to face the qibla on his right side, by analogy with the state of being placed in the grave, because that is more honorable for him. The chosen practice in our lands is laying on the back because it is easier for the soul to exit. The first is the Sunnah. And he is prompted with the two testimonies due to his saying: 'Prompt your dying ones with the testimony that there is no god but Allah.' What is meant is the one who is near death. Then when he dies, his jaw is bound and his eyes are closed. With this, inheritance follows. Then there is beautification in it, so it is recommended.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on how to treat a person at the time of death and immediately after. The author begins by stating that the dying person should be placed on his right side facing the qibla, analogizing to the position in the grave. However, he notes that in our lands (Transoxiana), the chosen practice is to lay him on his back because it is easier for the soul to leave. He clarifies that the first method (right side) is the Sunnah. Then he mentions talqin: prompting the dying person to say the shahada, based on the hadith 'Prompt your dying ones...' The 'dying ones' means those near death, not the already dead, because talqin would be useless for a corpse. After death, the jaw is bound and eyes are closed. This is the inherited practice, and beautifying the corpse is considered recommended (mustahsan). The ruling establishes that these actions are sunnah or mustahsan, not obligatory.

Key Terms
احتضر (ihtadara): To be on the verge of death; the state of dying.
القبلة (al-qiblah): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca, towards which the dying person is turned.
الاستلقاء (al-istilqa'): Laying on the back, an alternative position for the dying person chosen for ease in our lands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Because it prevents the face from turning away from the qibla.
D) Because it is the practice of the Sahaba.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends the right side facing qibla as Sunnah, but permits laying on the back for ease of dying.

Talqin and Post-Death Actions: Sunnah and Mustahsan
Rulings on talqin and post-death actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling of talqin and identify the actions after death that are mustahsan.

Core Idea
Talqin is a sunnah for the dying, not the dead; after death, binding the jaw and closing the eyes are mustahsan.

The Prophet ﷺ instructed us to prompt the dying with the shahada. But this is for those still alive, not the corpse. After death, certain actions are recommended to honor the deceased—binding the jaw and closing the eyes are part of the inherited tradition. Let's examine the evidence and rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Talqin: prompting the dying person to say 'La ilaha illallah' is a sunnah. Binding the jaw and closing the eyes are mustahsan (recommended).
The text states 'ولقن الشهادتين' and then 'فاذا مات شد لحياه وغمض عيناه'.
2
Locate the dalil for talqin
The hadith: 'لقنوا موتاكم شهادة ان لا اله الا الله' (Prompt your dying ones with the testimony...). The word 'موتاكم' here means those near death.
The author classifies this as a non-obligatory command, indicating sunnah.
3
Clarify the scope of talqin
Talqin is only for the one near death, not the already dead, because the purpose is to have the shahada be the final words.
The text explicitly says 'والمراد الذى قرب من الموت'.
4
Note the post-death actions
After death, binding the jaw and closing the eyes are done. These are mustahsan (beautification) based on the inherited practice.
The phrase 'بهذا جرى التوارث ثم فيه تحسينة فيستحسن' indicates they are recommended.

The Cause of Washing the Deceased: Hadath vs. Najasah
Examines two Hanafi views on why ghusl is required

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two Hanafi opinions on the cause of washing the deceased and explain why the ruling is fard kifayah.

Core Idea
The obligation to wash the deceased is unanimously fard kifayah, but the underlying cause (hadath or najasah) differs.

You already know that washing the deceased is an obligation upon the living community. But why is a full-body wash required, and not just the wudu limbs? This passage presents two explanations within the Hanafi school—one based on ritual impurity (hadath) and one based on physical impurity (najasah). Both lead to the same ruling, but the reasoning differs. Let’s examine each carefully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions on the cause
The passage first presents the opinion that the cause is hadath—a state of ritual impurity that settles in the body after death due to relaxation of muscles. Then it presents a second opinion that the cause is najasah—physical impurity analogous to dead animals.
Both opinions are found within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the first opinion (hadath) and its response to an objection
An objector asks: if it is hadath, why require a full wash when normally wudu suffices? The answer: in life, hadath recurs frequently; if full wash were required each time, it would cause hardship. But death-hadath occurs only once, so no hardship, thus full wash is required.
The response relies on the principle of repelling hardship (raf' al-haraj).
3
Analyze the second opinion (najasah) and its evidence
This opinion compares the dead human to a dead animal, which is najis. Evidence: carrying a dead human invalidates prayer, but carrying a person with hadath does not. Therefore, the dead human is najis, and impurity is removed by washing.
The passage notes that washing a dead animal does not purify it; purification of a dead human is due to honor (takrim).
4
Confirm the consensus ruling
The passage concludes by stating that washing the deceased is fard kifayah—a communal obligation—by consensus (bil-ittifaq).
Fard kifayah means if some Muslims perform it, the obligation is discharged for all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غسل میت کے سبب میں اختلاف ہے بعض نے کہا کہ غسل میت کا سبب وہ حدیث ہے جو استر خا و مفاصل کی وجہ سے میت کے اندر حلول کر گیا ہے کیونکہ موت کی وجہ سے انسان ناپاک نہیں ہوتا ہے رہا یہ کہ غسل میت کا سبب جب حدث ہے تو اعضاء وضو کے دھونے پر اکتفاء کیوں نہیں کیا گیا درانحالیکہ حدث کی صورت میں اعضاء وضو کے دھونے پر اکتفاء کیا جاتا ہے۔ جواب زندگی میں حدث کی وجہ سے اعضاء وضو پر اکتفاء کرنا دفع حرج کے لئے تھا اس لئے کہ حدث ہر روز پیش آتا ہے بلکہ ایک دن میں کئی بار پیش آتا ہے پس اگر زندگی میں اعضاء وضو کے دھونے پر اکتفانہ کیا جاتا بلکہ پورے بدن کا غسل ضروری ہوتا ہے تو لوگ حرج اور ضرر میں مبتلا ہو جاتے ۔ اس لئے زندگی میں حدث کی وجہ سے اعضا وضو دھونے پر اکتفاء کرنے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے اور رہاوہ حدث جومیت کی وجہ سے لاحق ہوتا ہے تو وہ مکرر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ایک ہی بار پیش آتا ہے پس چونکہ موت کی وجہ سے حدث ایک بار پیش آنے کی وجہ سے حرج اور ضرر کا احتمال نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں پورے بدن کے دھونے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے اور بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ غسل میت کا سبب میت کا موت کی وجہ سے نجس اور نا پاک ہونا ہے جیسے دوسرے حیوانات موت کی وجہ سے نجس ہو جاتے ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے مردہ انسان کو اپنے بدن پر لاد کر نماز پڑھی تو اس کی نماز جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر کسی محدث کو لا کر پڑھی تو اس کی نماز جائز ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مردہ انسان نجس ہے اور نجاست کا زوال غسل سے ہوتا ہے اس لئے غسل میت کو لازم قرار دیا گیا ہے یہ دھیان رہے کہ مردہ جانور کو اگر فنسل دیدیا گیا تو وہ پاک نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ مردہ انسان کا نسل کی وجہ سے پاک ہو جانا محض اس کی تکریم اور تعظیم کی وجہ سے ہے۔ غسل میت زندہ لوگوں پر بالا تفاق فرض علی الکفایہ ہے۔
There is a difference of opinion regarding the cause of washing the deceased. Some said that the cause of washing the deceased is the hadath that has settled inside the deceased due to relaxation of joints and muscles, because a human does not become impure by death. If it is said that the cause of washing the deceased is hadath, then why is it not sufficient to wash the limbs of wudu, just as in the case of hadath the washing of wudu limbs suffices? The answer is that in life, being content with washing the wudu limbs due to hadath was to repel hardship, because hadath occurs every day, rather several times a day. If in life washing the wudu limbs was not sufficient and a full body wash was required every time, people would fall into hardship and harm. Therefore, in life, the ruling of being content with washing the wudu limbs due to hadath was given. As for the hadath that occurs due to death, it does not recur; it occurs only once. Since the hadath due to death occurs only once, there is no likelihood of hardship and harm. Hence, in this case, the ruling of washing the entire body was given. And some scholars said that the cause of washing the deceased is that the deceased becomes najis and impure due to death, just as other animals become impure by death. The evidence is that if someone prays while carrying a dead human on his body, his prayer is not valid. But if he prays while carrying a person who has hadath, his prayer is valid. From this it is understood that a dead human is najis, and removal of impurity is through washing; therefore, washing the deceased was made obligatory. It should be noted that if a dead animal is washed, it does not become pure, because the purification of a dead human through washing is solely due to his honor and veneration. Washing the deceased is, by consensus, fard kifayah upon the living.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage discusses the reason (sabab) for the obligation of washing the deceased. It presents two opinions within the Hanafi school. First opinion: the cause is hadath (state of ritual impurity) that settles in the body after death due to relaxation of muscles. The objection is raised: if it is hadath, why is a full wash required when normally only the wudu limbs are washed? The answer: in life, hadath is frequent, so wudu suffices to avoid hardship; death-hadath occurs once, so no hardship, thus full wash is required. Second opinion: the cause is najasah (impurity) of the dead body, analogous to dead animals. Evidence: carrying a dead human invalidates prayer, while carrying a person in hadath does not. So the dead human is impure, and impurity is removed by washing. A clarification: washing a dead animal does not purify it; the purification of a dead human by washing is due to his honor (takrim). The passage concludes with the consensus ruling that washing the deceased is fard kifayah upon the living. The passage is a talil (reasoning) episode explaining the basis of the obligation.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): State of ritual impurity that requires wudu or ghusl; here argued to occur upon death due to relaxation of limbs.
نجاسة (najasah): Physical impurity (like blood, urine); some scholars consider the dead human as najis, requiring washing for purification.
فرض علی الکفایہ (fard ala al-kifayah): A communal obligation — if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved of sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence for the opinion that the cause of washing is najasah?
A) A hadith stating that the deceased is impure.
B) Carrying a dead human invalidates prayer, but carrying a person with hadath does not.
C) The deceased cannot perform wudu, so a full wash is needed.
D) The community consensus (ijma') that washing is required.

Key Takeaway
Washing the deceased is fard kifayah in all cases; the cause is debated between hadath and najasah, but both lead to the same obligation.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
9 min
Method of Washing the Deceased
Procedure and rulings for ghusl al-mayyit with detailed steps and a dispute on water temperature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for washing the deceased, including the preferred water temperature and sequence, and explain why warm water is preferred over cold.

Core Idea
Hanafi ghusl al-mayyit prioritizes effective cleansing: warm water and a three-stage water sequence (plain, sidr, camphor).

This lesson covers the detailed method of washing the deceased according to the Hanafi school. It addresses the obligation, the necessary steps before washing, the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding water temperature, the recommended sequence of waters, and the post-wash actions. By the end, you will be able to perform or guide the ghusl with proper knowledge of its rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Obligation and Pre-Wash Requirements
Recognize that ghusl al-mayyit is fard kifayah. Note the necessity of covering the private parts, performing wudu (without rinsing mouth/nose), and placing the body on a raised surface.
Wudu is sunnah but mouth and nose are omitted due to difficulty.
2
Understand the Water Temperature Dispute
Learn the Hanafi position (warm water) and the Shafi'i counter-argument (cold water). Understand the Hanafi response: warm water is more effective for cleansing and any expelled impurities come out during washing, not after.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
3
Learn the Recommended Sequence of Waters
Memorize the three-stage sequence: plain water (to wet), then sidr water (to cleanse), then camphor water (to perfume). This is based on the practice of angels with Prophet Adam and narrated from Ibn Mas'ud.
Sidr is preferred for its cleansing properties; camphor is for fragrance.
4
Describe the Washing Procedure
Explain that the body is washed on its left side to start from the right. Water is poured until it reaches the part touching the board. After the wash, the stomach is gently rubbed (based on 'Ali's action) to expel any remaining impurities.
If something exits after washing, it is washed off; ghusl is not repeated.
5
Note the Final Steps and Classification
After washing, the body is dried with a clean cloth. Understand the hierarchy: one complete wash fulfills the obligation (rukn); the three-stage sequence is sunnah; covering private parts is obligatory (shart).
The sunnah acts enhance the ghusl but are not required for validity.

فاذا اراد و اغسله وضعوه على سريد لينصب الماء عنه وجعلوا على عورته خرقة اقامة لواجب السترو يكتفى بستر العورة الغليظة هو الصحيح تيسيرا ونزعوا ثيابه ليمكنهم التنظيف ووضوه من غير مضمضة واستنشاق لان الوضوء سنة الاغتسال غير ان اخراج الماء منه متعذر فيتركان ثم يفيضون الماء عليه اعتبارا بحال الحيوية ويجمر سريره وترا لما فيه من تعظيم الميت وانما يوتر لقوله ان الله وتريحب الوتر،

کو اسکے بائیں پہلو پر لٹا کر جوش دیتے ہوئے پانی سے دھویا جائے اور اسقدر پانی ڈالا جائے کہ نیچے کا حصہ تو تختہ سے ملا ہوا ہے۔ اس تک پانی پہنچ جائے پھر یہ ترتیب اس لئے رکھی ہے تاکہ غسل کا دائیں پہلو سے شروع کرنا پایا جائے کیونکہ سنت ابتداء بالیمین ہے۔ پھر غسل دینے والا میت کو اپنے بدن سے ٹیک لگا کر بٹھلائے اور نرم انداز سے میت کے پیٹ کو ملے یہ ملنا اس لئے ہے کہ میت کے پیٹ میں اگر کوئی چیز ہو تو نکل اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور نہ وضو کے اعادہ کی ضرورت ہے۔ کیونکہ غسل میت کو ہم نے نص سے پہچانا ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسلمان کے مسلمان پر چھ حق ہیں ۔ ان میں سے ایک غسل میت ہے۔ بہر حال غسل میت جو واجب ہے ایک مرتبہ غسل دینے سے حاصل ہو گیا ہے۔ اب دوبارہ غسل دینے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ غسل سے فراغت کے بعد میت کے بدن کو پاک کپڑے سے صاف کر دیا جائے تا کہ کفن نہ بھیگے ۔
Method of washing the deceased. When they intend to wash him, they place him on a washing table so water can drain, and put a cloth on his private parts to fulfill the obligation of covering, and it is sufficient to cover the thick private parts, this is correct for ease. They remove his clothes to allow cleaning, and perform wudu for him without rinsing mouth and nose, because wudu is a sunnah of ghusl, but expelling water from them is difficult, so they are omitted. Then they pour water over him considering the state of living. They fumigate his bier with an odd number of incense due to reverence. The odd number is because the Prophet said, 'Allah is one and loves odd numbers.' Water is boiled [and used] because it is more effective for cleaning and purification. Imam al-Shafi'i says that it is better to use cold water for washing the deceased, because hot water loosens the body parts and causes impurity to exit, soiling the shroud. To avoid this, cold water is preferable. Our response is that washing the deceased is legislated for cleansing, and hot water is more effective for cleansing, so hot water is better. As for hot water loosening the limbs, we say this is actually helpful for cleansing, because whatever is in the stomach will come out during washing, so after washing the shroud is not soiled. If boiled water is not available, then plain water is used. The sequence of water according to Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi and Sheikh al-Islam and Sahib al-Muhit: first plain water, then water with sidr leaves boiled, then water with a bit of camphor. This is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: he said, 'Begin with pure water, then water with sidr, then water with camphor.' Pure water first to wet the dirt and impurity, then sidr water to remove dirt as sidr is more cleansing, then camphor water to perfume the body. The angels did this with Adam (peace be upon him) when they washed him. Quduri said: wash the head and beard of the deceased with 'ushn (a plant used like soap) because it cleanses like soap. After all this, lay the deceased on his left side and wash him with boiled water, pouring enough water to reach the part touching the board. This order is so that washing starts from the right side, as the sunnah is to begin with the right. Then the washer sits the deceased against his body and gently rubs the stomach to expel anything inside to avoid soiling the shroud. The basis for this is the narration that Ali (RA) when he washed the Prophet (SAW), he gently rubbed his stomach with his hand seeking what is sought from the deceased, and he saw nothing, and said, 'You are pure alive and dead.' If something comes out after rubbing, it is washed off and neither ghusl nor wudu is repeated. The obligation of ghusl is fulfilled with one wash. After washing, the body is dried with a clean cloth so the shroud does not get wet.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage details the method of washing the deceased according to the Hanafi school. It covers: placing the body on a table, covering the private parts, performing wudu (except rinsing mouth/nose), pouring water, using incense. A dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is addressed: Hanafis prefer hot water for effective cleansing, while Shafi'is prefer cold to avoid soiling the shroud. The Hanafi response notes that hot water helps expel impurities during washing. The sequence of waters is: plain water, then sidr water, then camphor water, as narrated from Ibn Mas'ud. Quduri adds washing the head and beard with 'ushn like soap. The body is washed on its left side to start from the right. After washing, the stomach is gently rubbed (based on the Prophet's washing by Ali) to expel anything; if something comes out, it is washed but ghusl is not repeated. The obligation is fulfilled with one wash. Finally, the body is dried.

Key Terms
سدر (sidr): Leaves of the lotus tree used for washing the deceased for cleansing.
كا فور (kafoor): Camphor, used in the third wash to perfume the body.
عظمی ('ushn): A plant used like soap to wash the head and beard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of washing the deceased prioritizes thorough cleansing using warm water and a specific sequence of water types, rooted in prophetic practice and the need for purification.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Hot Water and Washing Order for the Deceased
Debates water temperature and prescribes washing order with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on using hot water for ghusl al-mayyit, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi response using istihsan.

Core Idea
Hot water is preferable for ghusl al-mayyit because it better achieves cleansing, even if it softens limbs.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the temperature of water used to wash the deceased. The Hanafi school, relying on the principle of istihsan and the purpose of ghusl (cleansing), holds that hot water is preferable. The Shafi'i school, concerned about soiling the shroud, prefers cold water. We will also explore the sunnah order of washing as derived from the practice of the angels.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding water temperature for ghusl al-mayyit and the basis for it.
The position is that hot water is afdal (preferable) because it is more effective for cleansing (tanzif).
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds cold water is preferable and understand his concern about limbs softening and impurities soiling the shroud.
The Shafi'i proof is based on practicality: avoiding post-wash soiling.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i argument using istihsan and the purpose of ghusl.
The Hanafi response: impurities expelled during washing are removed then, preventing later soiling; softening helps this process.
4
Learn the sunnah washing order
Understand the prescribed sequence: pure water, sidr water, then camphor water, based on Ibn Mas'ud's narration and the angels' practice with Adam.
This order is considered sunnah muakkadah.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: Hanafis use hot water, Shafi'is use cold water. Both agree on the wajib nature of ghusl.
The dispute affects the recommended method, not the obligation.

نے کہا کہ میت کو غسل دیتے وقت خالص پانی سے ابتداء کیجائے پھر بیری کے پتوں سے جوش دیا ہوا پانی پھر کافور ملا ہوا پانی استعمال کیا جائے۔ اولاً خالص پانی تو اس لئے استعمال کرے تا کہ بدن کا میل اور نجاست و غیر بھیگ کر گل جائے پھر جوش دیا ہوا پانی اس لئے استعمال کرے کہ میل کچیل دور ہو جائے گا کیونکہ بیری کے پتے ابلغ فی التنظیف ہیں پھر کافور کا پانی بدن میت کو معطر اور خوشبو دار کرنے کے لئے استعمال کیا جائے ۔ یہی عمل ملائکہ نے آدم کو نسل دیتے وقت کیا تھا قدوری نے کہا کہ میت کے سر اور اس کی داڑھی کو عظمی سے دھویا جائے کیونکہ علمی صابن کی طرح بدن کو نظیف کرنے والی ہے۔ ان سب کاموں سے فراغت کے بعد میت کو اسکے بائیں پہلو پر لٹا کر جوش دیتے ہوئے پانی سے دھویا جائے اور اسقدر پانی ڈالا جائے کہ نیچے کا حصہ تو تختہ سے ملا ہوا ہے۔ اس تک پانی پہنچ جائے پھر یہ ترتیب اس لئے رکھی ہے تاکہ غسل کا دائیں پہلو سے شروع کرنا پایا جائے کیونکہ سنت ابتداء بالیمین ہے۔ پھر غسل دینے والا میت کو اپنے بدن سے ٹیک لگا کر بٹھلائے اور نرم انداز سے میت کے پیٹ کو ملے یہ ملنا اس لئے ہے کہ میت کے پیٹ میں اگر کوئی چیز ہو تو نکل آئے بعد میں کفن کو آلودہ نہ کرے۔ اس سلسلہ میں اصل یہ روایت ہے ان عليا لما غسل رسول الله مسح بطنه بيده رفيقاً طلب منه ما يطلب من الميت فلم ير شيئاً فقال طبت حياً وميتاً - یعنی حضرت علی نے
جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو مسل دیا تو اپنے ہاتھ سے آہستہ آہستہ آپ کا پیٹ ملا۔ اور مقصود اس چیز کو طلب کرنا تھا جو میت سے طلب کی جاتی ہے۔ یعنی حضرت علی کا منشاء یہ تھا کہ شاید آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پیٹ سے کوئی چیز نکل آئے لیکن کوئی چیز نہیں نکلی ۔ پھر حضرت علیؓ نے فرمایا کہ آپ تو جیتے بھی پاک ہیں اور مرتے بھی طبیب ہیں۔ پیٹ ملنے کے بعد اگر میت کے پیٹ سے کوئی چیز نکل آئی تو اس کو دھو ڈالے اور غسل کے اعادہ کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور نہ وضو کے اعادہ کی ضرورت ہے۔ کیونکہ غسل میت کو ہم نے نص سے پہچانا ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ مسلمان کے مسلمان پر چھ حق ہیں ۔ ان میں سے ایک غسل میت ہے۔ بہر حال غسل میت جو واجب ہے ایک مرتبہ غسل دینے سے حاصل ہو گیا ہے۔ اب دوبارہ غسل دینے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ غسل سے فراغت کے بعد میت کے بدن کو پاک کپڑے سے صاف کر دیا جائے تا کہ کفن نہ بھیگے ۔
Chapter of Funerals. ... (Explanation of the ruling on using hot water and the order of washing, with proofs from Ibn Mas'ud and the angels.)
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage begins with an inter-madhhab dispute regarding water temperature for washing the deceased. Imam Shafi'i holds cold water preferable to avoid softening limbs and soiling the shroud. The Hanafi response uses istihsan: ghusl aims at cleansing, and hot water is more effective. Any impurity expelled during washing is then removed, preventing later soiling. If hot water is unavailable, cold water suffices. Then the order of washing is prescribed: first pure water, then sidr (ber leaf) water, then camphor water, based on a narration from Ibn Mas'ud and the practice of angels washing Adam. After washing, the body is placed on its left side to begin with the right side (sunnah of starting with the right). The washer gently presses the stomach to expel any remaining impurities, as narrated from Ali washing the Prophet (peace be upon him). No repetition of ghusl or wudu is required if something emerges.

Key Terms
تنظيف (tanzif): Cleansing; the purpose of ghusl according to the Hanafi school.
سدر (sidr): Ber leaves used in washing the deceased for their cleansing property.
كافور (kafur): Camphor, used in the final wash for perfume and preservation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using hot water for washing the deceased?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah muakkadah.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Hot water is recommended for ghusl al-mayyit due to its superior cleansing, and any softening during washing actually prevents later soiling of the shroud.

Perfuming and Grooming the Deceased: Sunnah and Prohibition
Rulings on applying hanut and camphor, and forbidding combing and cutting hair/nails.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah rulings for applying hanut and camphor to the deceased and explain the prohibition of combing and cutting hair/nails, citing the primary proofs.

Core Idea
Perfuming the deceased is sunnah; grooming is prohibited because the deceased needs no adornment.

After washing and shrouding, the next steps involve perfuming the body. This passage from al-Hidayah explains which perfumes to apply and where, while also forbidding any grooming actions associated with the living. Understanding these rulings ensures proper funeral practice in accordance with the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of actions
The passage covers two sets: (a) positive sunnah of applying hanut on head/beard and camphor on prostration points; (b) negative prohibition of combing hair/beard and cutting nails/hair. Distinguish them clearly.
The prohibition is makruh tanzih, not haram.
2
For the sunnah, locate the proof
Find the hadith about the angels with Adam (bringing hanut and camphor) and the instruction of Umm Atiyya to use camphor in the final wash. Understand that these establish the sunnah.
The hadith is from al-Hakim and is considered zanni al-thubut.
3
Understand the reasoning behind the prohibition
The passage cites Aisha's question 'Why do you pull your deceased?' and the principle that combing/cutting are for adornment, which the deceased no longer needs. For the living, it was cleanliness; for the dead, it becomes like circumcision (not performed after death).
Circumcision is also not done for the deceased; analogy (qiyas) is used.
4
Note the legal status and ikhtilaf
Perfuming is sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended). The prohibition is makruh tanzih (disliked). Some other schools may allow cutting, but Hanafi prohibits it. Recognize that the evidence is based on a hadith (zanni) and analogy.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position as stated.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a funeral home: after bath, the body is perfumed with hanut on head/beard and camphor on prostration points. No combing or cutting of hair/nails occurs, even if family requests it.
This ensures the body is treated according to sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو برای جلد دوم
۳۴۷
اعضاء سجدہ میں خوشبو لگانے کا حکم ، میت کو کنگھی کرنے ، ناخن اور بال کاٹنے کا حکم
باب الجنائز
ويجعله اى الميت فى اكفانه ويجعل الحنوط على رأسه ولحيته والكافور على مساجده لان التطيب سنة والمساجد اولى بزيادة الكرامة ولا يسرح شعر الميت ولالحيته ولا يقص ظفره ولا شعره لقول عائشة علام تنصون ميتكم ولان هذه الاشياء للزينة وقد استغنى الميت عنها وفى الحى كان تنظيفا لاجتماع الوسخ تحتة وصار كالختان
ترجمہ اور میت کو اس کے کفن کے کپڑوں میں رکھ دے۔ اور میت کے سر اور داڑھی پر حنوط لگا دے اور اس کے اعضاء سجدہ پر کافور لگایا جائے کیونکہ خوشبو دار کرنا سنت ہے۔ اور اعضاء موجود زیادتی کرامت کے زیادہ لائق ہیں اور میت کے بال اور اس کی داڑھی میں کنکھی نہ کی جائے اور نہ اس کے ناخن کاٹے جائیں اور نہ بال کاٹے جائیں۔ کیونکہ حضرت اعائشہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ کس وجہ سے تم اپنے مردے کی پیشانی پکڑ کر کھینچتے ہو اور اس لئے کہ یہ چیزیں تو زینت کے واسطے ہیں۔ اور میت زینت سے بے پرواہ ہو چکا اور زندہ کے اندر نظافت تھی کیونکہ اس کے نیچے میل کچیل جمع ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ ختنہ کرنے کے مانند ہو گیا۔
تشریح میت کو غسل دینے کے بعد اس کو کفن پہنایا جائے اور میت کے سر اور داڑھی پر حنوط لگا دے۔ حنوط چند خوشبودار چیزوں سے مرکب عطر کا نام ہے اور جو اعضاء سجدہ میں زمین پر سکتے ہیں (پیشانی ، ناک، دونوں ہاتھ ، دونوں گھٹنے ، دونوں قدم ) ان پر کافور لگایا جائے دلیل یہ ہے کہ میت کے بدن کو خوشبو دار کرنا سنت ہے۔ اور چونکہ مذکورہ اعضاء پر سجدہ کیا جاتا ہے اس لئے اعضاء سجود کرامت کے زیادہ لائق ہیں۔ اور سنت ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کان آدم النبي رجلاً اشعر طوالاً كانه نخلة سحوق فلما حضره الموت نزلت الملائكة بحنوط و كفن من الجنة فلما مات عليه السلام غسلوه بالماء والسدر ثلاثاً و جعلوه في الثالثة كافوراً و كفنوه فى و ترمن الثياب و حفروا له لحداً و صلوا عليه و قالوا هذه سنة دلد آدم من بعده وفي رواية قالوا يا بنى آدم هذه سنتكم من بعده بكذا لكم فافعلوا انه رواه الحاکم (شرح نقایه ) حضور نے فرمایا ہے کہ آدم گھنے بالوں والے لانے قد والے انسان تھے ۔ گویا ایک بہت لانبا کھجور کا درخت ہے۔ پس جب موت کا وقت آیا تو فرشتے خوشبو اور جنت سے کفن لے کر اترے۔ پس جب آدم مر گئے تو فرشتوں نے آدم کو بیر کے پتوں سے جوش دیئے ہوئے پانی سے تین بار غسل دیا اور تیسری مرتبہ میں کافور لا گایا اور تین کپڑوں میں کفن دیا۔ اور ان کے لئے لحد ( قبر ) کھودی اور ان پر نماز جنازہ پڑھی اور کہا کہ آدم کے بعد یہ اولاد آدم کی سنت ہے، اور ایک روایت میں ہے کہ فرشتوں نے کہا کہ اے اولاد آدم ، آدم کے بعد یہ تمہاری سنت ہے اس طرح تم بھی کرنا اور ام عطیہ کی حدیث ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے واجعلن في الآخرة كافوروا او شيئاً من كافور یعنی آخر میں میت کے بدن کو کافور لگاؤ۔
امام قدوری نے کہا کہ میت کے نہ بالوں میں کنگھی کی جائے اور نہ داڑھی میں ۔ اور نہ اس کے ناخن کاٹے جائیں اور نہ بال دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عائشہ سے میت کے بالوں اور سکھی کرنے کے سلسلہ میں دریافت کیا گیا تو حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا عـلام تــنــصـون ميکم ، لفظ علام اصل میں علی ما ہے یعنی ما استفہامیہ پر علی حرف جر داخل کیا گیا ہے پھر اس کا الف گرادیا گیا۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کے قون
And he places the deceased in his shroud, and applies hanut on his head and beard, and camphor on his prostration points because perfuming is sunnah, and the prostration points are more deserving of additional honor. And do not comb the hair of the deceased nor his beard, nor cut his nails nor his hair, because of the saying of Aisha: 'Why do you pull your deceased?' and because these things are for adornment, and the deceased has no need of them...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage gives rulings after washing: the body is placed in the shroud, hanut (a compound perfume) is applied to the head and beard, and camphor is applied to the seven prostration points (forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet). Perfuming the body is sunnah, and the prostration points receive extra honor due to their role in worship. Then it forbids combing the hair or beard and cutting nails or hair, citing Aisha's question 'Why do you pull your deceased?' and the principle that these are acts of adornment, which the deceased no longer needs. For the living, such grooming was for cleanliness to prevent dirt accumulation, similar to circumcision (which is not done for the deceased). The proof for perfuming includes the hadith of the angels bringing hanut and camphor for Adam, and the hadith of Umm Atiyya instructing the use of camphor in the final wash.

Key Terms
حنوط (hanut): A compound perfume applied to the deceased's head and beard.
مساجد (masajid): The seven body parts that touch the ground during prostration (forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet).
سرح (sarh): Combing the hair; prohibited after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT permissible for the deceased according to the passage?
A) Applying hanut on the head
B) Cutting the nails
C) Placing camphor on the prostration points
D) Wrapping in a shroud

Key Takeaway
Perfuming the deceased with hanut and camphor is sunnah; combing and cutting are prohibited because the deceased no longer needs adornment.

Grooming and Circumcision of the Deceased
Ruling on grooming and circumcision for the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on combing the hair of the deceased and on circumcising an uncircumcised deceased, and identify the proofs cited.

Core Idea
The deceased has no need for adornment; combing is disliked and circumcision is not performed by consensus.

When a loved one passes away, family members often wish to ensure the deceased appears well-groomed. However, Islamic law distinguishes between needs of the living and the dead. This lesson examines two specific acts: combing the hair and circumcision of the deceased, drawing from the precedent of Aisha (RA) and the principle that worldly adornment ceases at death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and rulings
The passage discusses two actions: combing the hair of the deceased and circumcising an uncircumcised deceased. The ruling for combing is makruh tanzih (mildly disliked), and circumcision is not performed (effectively haram) by consensus.
Note the nuance: combing is disliked but not sinful if done; circumcision is impermissible.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The text cites Aisha's (RA) disapproval of grabbing the forehead (i.e., combing). Her response indicates the act is not recommended. This hadith is the primary dalil.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), providing zanni certainty.
3
Analyze the reasoning from adornment
The second proof is rational: these acts are for adornment, and the deceased no longer needs adornment. This distinguishes them from the living, for whom grooming is permitted due to hygiene.
This is a qiyas-like argument based on the removal of need.
4
Note the consensus on circumcision
The text explicitly states that there is consensus (ittifaq) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools that circumcision of the deceased is not performed. This strengthens the ruling.
Consensus (ijma) is a strong proof, but here it is limited to these two major schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسالون میں ہے۔ نصا ينصو نصواً معنی ہیں پیشانی پکڑ کر کھینچتا، بہر حال حضرت عائشہ نے جواب میں فرمایا کہ تم اپنے مردہ کی پیشانی پکر کر کیوں کھینچتے ہو۔ گویا حضرت عائشہ نے مردے کے بالوں میں کنگھی کرنے پر ناراضگی اور ناگواری کا اظہار فرمایا ہے اور کمی کرنے کو پیشانی پکڑ کر کھینچنے کے ساتھ تعبیر فرمایا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تمام باتیں زینت کے لئے ہیں اور مردہ زیب و زینت سے بے پرواہ ہو چکا ہے۔ اس لئے ان چیزوں کی قطعاً ضرورت نہیں اور رہا زندہ لوگوں کا ان چیزوں پر عمل پیرا ہونا تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ناخن اور بال وغیرہ کے نیچے میل کچیل جمع ہونے کی وجہ سے از راہ نظافت ان کو اس کی اجازت دی گئی ہے اور یہ ختنہ کے مانند ہو گیا ہے چنانچہ زندہ آدمی کا ختنہ مسنون ہے اور مردہ اگر بغیر ختنہ تھا، تو ہمارے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک بالا تفاق ختنہ نہیں کیا جائے گا ، واللہ العلم - جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
In 'Yasalun' it is said: 'Nasa yansu naswan' meaning to grab the forehead and pull. Nevertheless, Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) replied: Why do you grab the forehead of your deceased and pull? Thus Aisha expressed displeasure and aversion towards combing the hair of the deceased, and she described the act of combing as grabbing the forehead and pulling. The second proof is that all these actions are for adornment, and the deceased is free from adornment. Therefore, these things are absolutely unnecessary. As for living people's practice of these things, the reason is that dirt accumulates under nails and hair, so they are permitted for cleanliness, and it has become like circumcision. Thus, circumcision for a living person is sunnah, but if the deceased was uncircumcised, according to us and Imam Shafi'i, by consensus, circumcision will not be performed. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah forgive him.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on two matters: combing the hair of the deceased and circumcision of the deceased. It begins by referencing a hadith where Aisha (RA) disapproved of combing the deceased's hair, likening it to pulling the forehead. The author then gives a second proof that such acts are for adornment, which the deceased no longer needs. Living people perform them for hygiene, but that need ends at death. The passage then discusses circumcision: while it is sunnah for the living, it is not performed on the deceased by consensus between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The ruling is clear: do not groom or circumcise the deceased.

Key Terms
نصو (nasw): In this context, it means to grab the forehead and pull, used figuratively for combing hair.
ختنہ (khitan): Circumcision; for the deceased it is not performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on circumcising a deceased man who was uncircumcised according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is sunnah to circumcise him
B) It is permissible but not sunnah
C) It is not done by consensus with the Shafi'i school
D) It is wajib if he was negligent

Key Takeaway
Acts of grooming for adornment are disliked for the deceased; circumcision is not performed by consensus.

The Woman's Shroud: Recommended and Sufficient Garments
Ruling on woman's shroud with proof from hadith and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah and sufficient (kifayah) number of garments for a woman's shroud, explain the proofs, and apply the ruling to scenarios of necessity.

Core Idea
Five garments are sunnah for a woman's shroud; three suffice; fewer is makruh without necessity.

Shrouding the deceased is an obligation, but the number of garments varies by recommendation and necessity. This lesson clarifies that for women, the complete sunnah is five garments, based on the Prophet's action for his daughter Zaynab. However, three garments (izar, lifafah, odhni) are sufficient. Using fewer than three is disliked (makruh tanzih) unless there is a genuine need. A similar principle applies to men, as shown in the hadith of Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish sunnah from kifayah
Identify that the author presents two levels: the complete recommended (sunnah) shroud of five garments and the minimal sufficient (kifayah) shroud of three garments.
The term kifayah refers to what fulfills the obligation.
2
Examine the proof for five garments
Read the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah: the Prophet provided five garments for his daughter Zaynab's shroud. This fi'l (action) indicates recommendation (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
Also note the rational analogy (qiyas) to her life practice.
3
Understand the sufficient shroud
The author lists the three garments: izar (waist-wrap), lifafah (large sheet), and odhni (head cover). These conceal the body adequately.
Three is the minimum; less is only permissible with necessity.
4
Analyze the ruling on fewer than three
Without necessity, using fewer than three is makruh tanzih (disliked). With necessity, it is ja'iz (permissible). The same principle applies to men: one garment suffices in necessity.
Necessity could include poverty or lack of cloth.
5
Apply the hadith of Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr
The Prophet allowed covering Mus'ab's head with a single cloak and placing grass on his feet due to insufficient cloth. This shows that necessity permits less than the sunnah.
This is a dalil for the male shroud of necessity.

(5) The band with which her breasts are tied, i.e., a breast band. The proof is the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah: when the Prophet's daughter Zaynab died, the women who washed her were given these five garments by the Prophet for her shroud. The rational proof is that in life a woman generally wears five garments; by analogy, after death she is also given five garments. 'And if they suffice with three garments' – here the sufficient shroud for a woman is mentioned. The sufficient shroud for a woman is three garments: (1) izar (lower wrap), (2) lifafah (sheet), (3) odhni (head cover). To shroud a woman in fewer than three garments is makruh if without necessity, otherwise permissible, and this is called a shroud of necessity. Similarly, for a man, being content with one garment is makruh, but if due to necessity it is permissible; one garment is a man's shroud of necessity. The proof is the hadith of Khabbab ibn al-Arat: 'He said: We migrated with the Prophet seeking the face of Allah, so our reward is with Allah. Among us, some passed away without taking any of their reward, among them Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr who was killed on the day of Uhud. He left only a namirah (striped cloak). When we covered his head with it, his feet were exposed, and when we covered his feet, his head was exposed. So the Messenger of Allah commanded us to cover his head and to put some idhkhir grass on his feet.'
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on the woman's shroud, distinguishing between the recommended (sunnah) and the sufficient (kifaya). The author begins by referring to the fifth item of the woman's shroud—a band to bind the chest—using the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah that the Prophet gave five garments for his daughter Zaynab's shroud. This establishes the sunnah. A rational analogy from life is added for support. The text then moves to the sufficient shroud (kafan kifaya) of three garments: izar (lower wrap), lifafah (outer sheet), and odhni (head cover). Using fewer than three is makruh tanzih without necessity but permissible when needed. For men, the same principle applies: one garment suffices in necessity, proven by the well-known hadith of Khabbab about Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr, where the Prophet ordered covering his head and placing grass on his feet due to the insufficient cloth. This shows that necessity permits less than the full sunnah shroud.

Key Terms
كفن (kafan): Shroud or burial garment for the deceased.
كفاية (kifayah): Sufficiency; the minimum that fulfills the obligation of shrouding.
ازار (izar): A lower wrap covering from waist to feet.
لفافہ (lifafah): A large sheet that covers the entire body.
اوڑھی (odhni): A head cover for women, similar to a khimar.

Key Takeaway
For a woman's shroud, five garments are sunnah, three are sufficient, and fewer than three are permissible only with necessity.

Method of Dressing and Perfuming the Shroud
Describes the order of dressing a deceased woman and the sunnah of perfuming the shroud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of dressing a deceased woman and explain the ruling on perfuming the shroud as sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Perfume the shroud with an odd number of incense; dress a woman: shift, braids over chest, khimar, then izar under lifafah.

This lesson covers two practical sunnahs in preparing a deceased woman's shroud: the order of dressing and the perfuming of the shrouds. The Hanafi school follows the practice of the Prophet for his daughter. Understanding these details ensures proper respect for the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the garments for a deceased woman
Locate the four main pieces: dir' (shift), khimar (headcover), izar (lower wrap), and lifafah (large sheet). Note the braiding of hair.
The text mentions hair placed as two braids (dafiratayn) on the chest.
2
Arrange the order of dressing
From the text: first dir', then hair braids over the dir' on chest, then khimar over that, then izar under the lifafah.
The lifafah is the outermost wrap; the izar is placed underneath it.
3
Understand the ruling on perfuming
The text states that the shrouds should be perfumed with incense (ijmar) an odd number of times before wrapping the body. This is based on the Prophet's command for his daughter.
The Arabic 'witr' means odd, emphasizing an odd count (e.g., 1, 3, 5).
4
Note the obligation of funeral prayer after shrouding
After finishing the shroud, the funeral prayer is performed, as it is a fard kifayah.

And the woman is dressed first in a shift (dir'), then her hair is made into two braids placed over her chest on top of the shift, then the head veil (khimar) over that, then the izar under the lifafah (large sheet). Translation: And for women, first a shirt is put on, then her hair is made into two braids and placed over the shirt on the chest, then the head cover over that, then the izar under the lifafah. Commentary: The phrase is clear. The ruling on perfuming the shrouds: He said: 'And the shrouds are perfumed with incense an odd number of times before the deceased is wrapped in them, because he [the Prophet] commanded perfuming his daughter's shrouds with an odd number. And al-ijmar is perfuming. Then when they finish that, they pray over him, because it [the prayer] is an obligation.' Translation: He said that before the deceased is placed in the shrouds, the shrouds should be fumigated with incense an odd number of times, because the Messenger of Allah commanded perfuming his daughter's shrouds with an odd number. And al-ijmar means making fragrant. Then when they finish that, they pray over the deceased, because the prayer is an obligation. Commentary: In this phrase, the ruling of fumigating the shrouds is mentioned. Al-ijmar (fumigation) means making fragrant. Fumigation with an odd number is sunnah, as the hadith witnesses. After finishing the shroud, the funeral prayer is performed over him, because the funeral prayer is fard kifayah.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage consists of two practical rulings. First, the method of dressing a deceased woman: the order is to put on the shirt (dir'), then braid her hair and place it on the chest over the shirt, then the head cover (khimar), then the izar (lower wrap) under the lifafah (large covering sheet). This order ensures modesty and proper wrapping. Second, the ruling on perfuming the shrouds: it is sunnah to incense the shrouds an odd number of times before wrapping the body, based on the Prophet's command for his daughter. The Arabic word 'ijmar' means perfuming with incense. After the shroud is completed, the funeral prayer is offered immediately. The commentary clarifies that the fumigation is sunnah muakkadah, and the prayer after is fard kifayah (communal obligation).

Key Terms
درع (dir'): A shift or chemise, a shirt-like garment that covers the upper body.
ضفيرتين (dafiratayn): Two braids of hair.
خمار (khimar): A head covering or veil that also covers the chest.
اجمار (ijmar): Perfuming with incense or fumigation.
وترا (witr): Odd number; the number of times the shrouds are fumigated.

Minimal Burial of a Non-Muslim Relative: Washing, Shrouding, and Burying without Islamic Rites
Ruling with proof from the Abu Talib incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing and burying a deceased non-Muslim relative when only a Muslim is available, and explain the proof from the incident of Abu Talib.

Core Idea
A Muslim may wash and bury a non-Muslim relative, but only with minimal acts—no ritual ghusl, no janaza prayer.

When a non-Muslim dies and only a Muslim relative is present, what should be done? The Hanafi school permits the Muslim to handle the burial, but with essential acts only. This ruling is based on the Prophet’s command to Ali regarding Abu Talib. In this lesson, you will examine the specific conditions and the limiting proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing, shrouding, and burying a deceased non-Muslim by a Muslim relative. The ruling is permissible (mubah) with a minimal method.
Not fard or sunnah; merely permitted when necessary.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith where the Prophet commanded Ali to wash, shroud, and bury Abu Talib, but prohibited initiating any matter (interpreted as no prayer or sunnah rites).
اغسله و گفته و واره ولا تحدث به حدثا حتى تلقانی
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command shows permissibility; the prohibition of 'حدثا' indicates exclusion of Islamic funeral rites.
حدثا here refers to any act beyond washing, shrouding, and burying.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may prohibit entirely; Hanafis allow it due to kinship necessity.
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is the minimal burial without sunnah, based on the clear hadith.
Mufta bihi: the ruling as stated.
